**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is July, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Later, Elon Musk left DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

The r/politics subreddit on Reddit is a community focused on discussing and sharing news, analysis, and commentary related to U.S. politics. It's primarily a hub for:

**TOP SECRET // CONGRESSIONAL LEADERSHIP EYES ONLY**

**DAILY BRIEFING – July 26, 2025**

**CHIEF NEWS ANALYST**

**Overview:** The political landscape is defined by an aggressive expansion of executive power, creating significant friction with the judiciary and generating what sources describe as a "culture of fear" within federal law enforcement. Major policy shifts on immigration, including redefining access to federal programs and a new executive order on birthright citizenship, are facing immediate and successful legal challenges. Simultaneously, direct threats against the President from foreign actors and unconventional diplomatic nominations are elevating national security concerns. At the state level, partisan battles over gerrymandering, education, and social policy are intensifying. Within Congress, traditional party discipline shows signs of fracturing, with unusual cross-party commentary and internal dissent on nominations and key legislation, signaling a volatile and unpredictable legislative environment.

### **Area 1: The Trump Administration & Executive Branch**

**Topic 1.1: Immigration & Border Security**
The administration is executing a significant policy shift to restrict non-citizen access to federal programs. The Department of Health and Human Services, under Secretary Robert F. Kennedy Jr., has formally banned "Illegal Aliens" from its taxpayer-funded programs [1] and moved to redefine Clinton-era guidance, an action aimed at removing thousands of undocumented children from the low-income Head Start pre-K program [2]. These administrative actions are occurring alongside a new executive order on birthright citizenship, which has generated uncertainty for immigrant families [3]. Enforcement actions are also drawing sharp scrutiny. In the case of Kilmar Abrego Garcia, the administration has stated its intent to deport him before trial if he is released [4], yet an ICE official testified that the government does not know to which country he would be sent [5]. A separate incident is also drawing attention, wherein ICE agents reportedly handcuffed a 71-year-old U.S. citizen at an immigration court in San Diego [6].

[1] HHS Bans Illegal Aliens from Accessing its Taxpayer-Funded Programs, https://www.hhs.gov/press-room/prwora-hhs-bans-illegal-aliens-accessing-taxpayer-funded-programs.html

[2] RFK Jr moves to kick thousands of undocumented kids off low-income Head Start pre-K program | Federal health agency has redefined Clinton-era guidance that allowed undocumented people to access certain federal programs, https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/americas/us-politics/rfk-jr-pre-k-program-head-start-undocumented-children-b2786806.html

**Topic 1.2: Justice Department & Federal Law Enforcement**
Reports from multiple media outlets indicate a significant cultural and operational upheaval within federal law enforcement agencies. Sources describe a pervasive "culture of fear" at both the Justice Department and the FBI, where firings are allegedly occurring without explanation [1]. The F.B.I. is reportedly deploying polygraph tests to assess the loyalty of its officials, a highly unusual measure [2]. In what one publication labels a "pure act of retribution," the F.B.I. is also said to be investigating former directors of both the CIA and the FBI [3]. These internal dynamics are compounded by a whistleblower's claim, which a top Judiciary Democrat states is now backed by documents, that a senior DOJ official intended to defy court orders [4]. This internal climate is having external repercussions, as nearly half of all U.S. election officials now express concern about the prospect of politically motivated investigations, a tactic the President has reportedly signaled he is open to pursuing [5].

**Topic 1.3: Agency Operations & Personnel**
Federal agencies are undergoing transformative changes in authority and leadership conduct. The Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE) has reportedly secured expanded access to sensitive government data and now holds the authority to "cut off billions to farmers" [1]. At the State Department, personnel have been put on formal notice that firings will commence "soon" [2]. Meanwhile, DHS Secretary Kristi Noem is facing sharp public criticism for her actions during the recent Texas floods. Reports allege she prioritized taking Instagram pictures and delayed FEMA aid requests, leading one outlet to label her "ICE Barbie" [3].

### **Area 2: Legal & Judicial Affairs**

**Topic 2.1: Court Rulings & Legal Precedents**
The judiciary has delivered significant rebukes to administration policy and actions related to January 6, 2021. A federal judge issued a nationwide injunction blocking President Trump's executive order on birthright citizenship. In his ruling, the judge stated it was "'Just not a close call'" and certified a class that includes both children and unborn children, a major victory for the ACLU [1]. In a separate matter, Supreme Court Justice Elena Kagan has declined to shield police officers who attended the 'Stop the Steal' rally from legal proceedings, allowing civil suits against them to move forward [2].

*References:*

**Topic 2.2: High-Profile Investigations & Lawsuits**
Legal challenges against President Trump continue to progress, with courts delivering key rulings. An appeals court has upheld the $5 million verdict against the President in the E. Jean Carroll sexual abuse and defamation lawsuit, dealing a legal blow [1]. Separately, attorney Alan Dershowitz has claimed he knows names on the Jeffrey Epstein client list but is "bound by confidentiality" [2].

**Topic 2.3: State-Level Legal Actions**
The administration is engaged in legal conflicts with state governments over regulatory and statutory authority. A federal lawsuit has been filed against California, with the administration arguing that the state's animal cruelty laws are the cause of high egg prices [1]. In New York, gun manufacturers have lost an appeal against the state's public nuisance law, a setback for the industry [2]. Meanwhile, Oklahoma is being sued again over a state mandate requiring its public schools to teach Bible stories and election conspiracy theories, continuing a legal battle over curriculum [3].

### **Area 3: Economic & Fiscal Policy**

**Topic 3.1: Federal Budget & Economic Oversight**
The administration's fiscal policy is marked by open tension with the Federal Reserve and a dual strategy of targeted spending cuts and potential tax reductions. The White House has taken the unusual step of publicly accusing Federal Reserve Chair Jerome Powell of mismanaging the central bank, citing the cost of a headquarters renovation project as a specific point of failure [1]. On the fiscal front, millions in agriculture funding for Western states, including for ranchers and farmers in Colorado, have been canceled by the administration [2]. These spending cuts occur as conservative groups simultaneously lobby President Trump to pursue another major tax cut [3]. These moves are set against a backdrop of concern, with at least one source arguing that a recent "GOP megabill" is a key driver of rising national debt for future generations [4].

**Topic 3.2: Trade & Tariffs**
Tariffs remain a central and controversial tool of the administration's economic and foreign policy. A newly imposed tariff on copper has been sharply criticized in one report as a "pointlessly disastrous" measure, signaling potential economic blowback [1]. Concurrently, President Trump is being accused of "mixing in politics" with trade policy. Reports claim he used the announcement of tariffs on Brazil to simultaneously criticize the ongoing investigation into that country's former president, Jair Bolsonaro, blurring the lines between economic and political objectives [2].

### **Area 4: National Security & Foreign Affairs**

**Topic 4.1: Foreign Aid, Sanctions & International Law**
U.S. foreign policy is being shaped by an assertive sanctions posture and contentious internal debate over foreign aid. In a highly unusual action, the U.S. government has imposed sanctions on Francesca Albanese, a United Nations Special Rapporteur, representing a significant departure from diplomatic norms and potentially straining relations with the UN [1]. On a separate track, a fissure is apparent in the Republican coalition over foreign aid, as Rep. Marjorie Taylor Greene is publicly urging Congress to terminate military aid to Israel. She argues Israel is a "'nuclear-armed'" and "'not a helpless country'" and thus should not receive U.S. military funding [2].

**Topic 4.2: Geopolitical Threats & Diplomacy**
A direct, public threat has been made against the President. An Iranian cleric has reportedly offered a monetary reward for anyone who "'brings the head of Trump'," a significant and overt threat requiring immediate intelligence and security assessment [1]. In diplomatic affairs, relations with a key northern ally appear strained, as travel between the U.S. and Canada has reportedly "plummeted" in both directions [2]. In a widely discussed move, the administration has nominated Nick Adams, a social media influencer and self-described "'alpha male'," to be the U.S. ambassador to Malaysia [3], a choice that has drawn sharp media criticism for his public persona [4].

### **Area 5: State & Local Governance**

**Topic 5.1: Texas Political Developments**
Texas is a central arena for intense political conflict. Governor Greg Abbott is facing accusations that he is doing President Trump's "bidding" by using a special session called during a flood crisis to advance a new gerrymandering plan [1]. Critics have labeled the move a "'partisan power grab'" divorced from the state's immediate needs [2]. Concurrently, a major personal development has impacted the state's leadership: State Senator Angela Paxton has filed for divorce from Texas Attorney General Ken Paxton [3], with one report specifying the filing was made "on biblical grounds" [4].

### **Area 6: Domestic Issues & Public Discourse**

**Topic 6.1: Education, Culture, & Civil Liberties**
Cultural debates are actively shaping public policy from the state to the federal level. In education, a "Red state" has mandated a PragerU-backed "'America First' test" for new teachers, specifically targeting those from states deemed "'woke'" [1]. At the federal level, the Trump administration has launched an investigation into the Diversity, Equity, and Inclusion (DEI) policies at George Mason University [2]. On civil liberties, new DHS guidance reportedly classifies common protest activities like using "skateboards and livestreams" as "'violent tactics'," raising concerns among civil rights advocates [3]. DAILY BRIEFING

The political landscape is defined by an aggressive expansion of executive power, creating significant friction with the judiciary and generating what sources describe as a "culture of fear" within federal law enforcement [195]. Major policy shifts on immigration, including redefining access to federal programs and a new executive order on birthright citizenship, are facing immediate and successful legal challenges [199]. Simultaneously, direct threats against the President from foreign actors [232] and unconventional diplomatic nominations [226] are elevating national security concerns. At the state level, partisan battles over gerrymandering, education, and social policy are intensifying. Within Congress, traditional party discipline shows signs of fracturing, with unusual cross-party commentary [212, 238] and internal dissent on nominations and key legislation [196, 222], signaling a volatile and unpredictable legislative environment.

## 1. The Trump Administration & Executive Branch

### 1.1 Immigration & Border Security
The administration is executing a significant policy shift to restrict non-citizen access to federal programs. The Department of Health and Human Services, under Secretary Robert F. Kennedy Jr., has formally banned "Illegal Aliens" from its taxpayer-funded programs [200] and moved to redefine Clinton-era guidance, an action aimed at removing thousands of undocumented children from the low-income Head Start pre-K program [272]. These administrative actions are occurring alongside a new executive order on birthright citizenship, which has generated uncertainty for immigrant families [260]. Enforcement actions are also drawing sharp scrutiny. In the case of Kilmar Abrego Garcia, the administration has stated its intent to deport him before trial if he is released [242], yet an ICE official testified that the government does not know to which country he would be sent [218]. A separate incident is also drawing attention, wherein ICE agents reportedly handcuffed a 71-year-old U.S. citizen at an immigration court in San Diego [229].

These internal dynamics are compounded by a whistleblower's claim, which a top Judiciary Democrat states is now backed by documents, that a senior DOJ official intended to defy court orders [243].
